                                                                                                                                                     have told you that
                                                                                                                              air is an elastic fluid.       Now it   is the
                                                                                                                              nature of all elastic bodies to yield to
                                                                                                                              pressure, and to endeavour to regain
                                                                                                                              their former figure as soon         as    the
                                                                                                                              pressure is taken      off".   In projecting
                                                                                                                              an arrow from your how, you exert
                                                                                                                              your strength to bring the two ends
                                                                                                                              of   the   bow nearer together, but the

                                                                                                                              covers its former shape: the power
                                                                                                                              by which      this is effected     is called
                                                                                                                              elasticity.

                                                                                                                          12 is 144,           and the square of 4 is 16,
Generated for acobblah (University of Michigan) on 2015-08-10 15:12 GMT / http://hdl.handle.net/2027/hvd.32044102874096

                                                                                                                          of   the funnel is to that of the tube as
                                                                                                                          144 to 167

                                                                                                                          by 16 without leaving a remainder.

                                                                                                                                                     I
                                                                                                                          would imagine. — will now give you
                                                                                                                          some rules for judging of, and pre
                                                                                                                          dicting,       the    state     of the weather,
                                                                                                                          which are taken                from writers who
                                                                                                                          have paid the most attention to these
Public Domain, Google-digitized / http://www.hathitrust.org/access_use#pd-google
                                                                                                                          subjects, and which my own observa
                                                                                                                          tions have verified.
                                                                                                                             1 .   The rising of the mercury pre
                                                                                                                          sages, in      general,        fair weather, and

                                                                                                                                    RULES FOR THE WEATHER.                    249
                                                                                                                          its falling foul weather, as rain, snow,
                                                                                                                          high winds,      and storms.       When
                                                                                                                          the surface of the mercury is convex,
                                                                                                                          or stands higher in             the middle          than
                                                                                                                          at the sides,        it is   a sign the mercury
                                                                                                                          is then in a rising state           ;    but   if    the
                                                                                                                          surface be concave or hollow in the
                                                                                                                          middle, it is then sinking.
Generated for acobblah (University of Michigan) on 2015-08-10 15:12 GMT / http://hdl.handle.net/2027/hvd.32044102874096
                                                                                                                               2.       In very hot weather,       the falling
                                                                                                                          of   the mercury indicates thunder.                  '   .
                                                                                                                               3.       In winter,     the rising      presages
                                                                                                                          frost     :    and in frosty weather,          if    the
                                                                                                                          mercury falls three or four divisions,
                                                                                                                          there will be a thaw.              But in a con
                                                                                                                          tinued frost,        if    the mercury rises,            it
                                                                                                                          will certainly snow.
                                                                                                                               4.       When     wet weather
Public Domain, Google-digitized / http://www.hathitrust.org/access_use#pd-google
                                                                                                                                                                       happens
                                                                                                                          soon after the depression               of   the mer
                                                                                                                          cury, expect but little of it; on the
                                                                                                                          contrary, expect but little fair wea
                                                                                                                          ther when it proves        shortly after
                                                                                                                                               fair(
                                                                                                                          the mercury has risen.           :
                                                                                                                                                              '^r

                                                                                                                          250              PNEUMATICS.
                                                                                                                            5. In wet weather, when the mer
                                                                                                                          cury rises much and high, and so
                                                                                                                          continues for two or three days be
                                                                                                                          fore the bad weather is entirely over,
                                                                                                                          then   a continuance      of fair weather
                                                                                                                          may be expected.
                                                                                                                            6.   In   fair weather, when the mer
                                                                                                                          cury falls much arid low, and thus
Generated for acobblah (University of Michigan) on 2015-08-10 15:12 GMT / http://hdl.handle.net/2027/hvd.32044102874096
                                                                                                                          continues for two or three days be
                                                                                                                          fore the rain comes, then a deal of
                                                                                                                          wet may be expected, and probably
                                                                                                                          high winds.
                                                                                                                            7.   The unsettled motion of the
                                                                                                                          mercury denotes unsettled weather.
                                                                                                                            8.   The words engraved on                the
                                                                                                                          scale are not so much to be attended
                                                                                                                          to as the rising      and        falling of the
Public Domain, Google-digitized / http://www.hathitrust.org/access_use#pd-google
                                                                                                                          mercury     :   for if it stand       at   much
                                                                                                                          rain, and then rises to changeable,
                                                                                                                          it denotes fair weather, though not to
                                                                                                                          continue so long as         if    the mercury
                                                                                                                          had risen higher.        If       the mercury

                                                                                                                               RULES FOR THE WEATHER.                    251
                                                                                                                          stands at fair, and falls to changeable,
                                                                                                                          bad weather may be expected.
                                                                                                                            9. In winter, spring,, and autumn,
                                                                                                                          the sudden      falling of the mercury,
                                                                                                                          and that for a large space,            denotes
                                                                                                                          high winds and storms     ;       but in sum
                                                                                                                          mer it presages heavy showers, and
                                                                                                                          often thunder.    It always       sinks lowest
                                                                                                                          of all for great winds, though not
Generated for acobblah (University of Michigan) on 2015-08-10 15:12 GMT / http://hdl.handle.net/2027/hvd.32044102874096
                                                                                                                          accompanied      with rain    ;    but it falls
                                                                                                                          more for wind and rain together than
                                                                                                                                                                               ,
                                                                                                                          for either of them alone.              .   ,
                                                                                                                             10.   If
                                                                                                                                   after rain the wind change
                                                                                                                          into any part of the north, with a
                                                                                                                          clear and dry sky, and the mercury rise,
                                                                                                                          it is a certain sign of fair weather.
                                                                                                                             11.   After very great           storms       of
Public Domain, Google-digitized / http://www.hathitrust.org/access_use#pd-google
                                                                                                                          wind,    when    the mercury has           been
                                                                                                                          low, it commonly rises again very fast.
                                                                                                                          In settled fair weather, except the ba
                                                                                                                          rometer sink much, expect but little

                                                                                                                                                  PKEUMAT1CS.
                                                                                                                              rain.       In   a wet season,          the smallest
                                                                                                                              depressions must be attended to             for     ;
                                                                                                                              when the air is               much inclined to
                                                                                                                              showers, a little sinking in the ba
                                                                                                                              rometer denotes more rain.                        And in
                                                                                                                              such a season,           if it   rise suddenly fast
                                                                                                                              and high, fair weather cannot be ex
                                                                                                                              pected to last more than a day or two.
                                                                                                                                 1   2.   The greatest heights                  of the
Generated for acobblah (University of Michigan) on 2015-08-10 15:12 GMT / http://hdl.handle.net/2027/hvd.32044102874096
